        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1876346788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3954541205217967600"><i>( 3.5 ) I wasn't quite sure what to expect going into this. The blurb kind of made it sound like there was going to be a little bit of a thriller / mystical element to this book, but it seemed to be a little watered down. Hence the reason I've created a shelf called 'middle grade' as it seems to fit that category a little better than young adult. Having said that, it was a really cute story!</i><br/><br/>What I Liked<br/><blockquote>1. The way the <b>blindness is handled</b>. It's mentioned in the book, sure, but not in a way that w</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3954541205217967600" style="display:none"><i>( 3.5 ) I wasn't quite sure what to expect going into this. The blurb kind of made it sound like there was going to be a little bit of a thriller / mystical element to this book, but it seemed to be a little watered down. Hence the reason I've created a shelf called 'middle grade' as it seems to fit that category a little better than young adult. Having said that, it was a really cute story!</i><br /><br />What I Liked<br /><blockquote>1. The way the <b>blindness is handled</b>. It's mentioned in the book, sure, but not in a way that would make a younger child think that anything was truly troubling about her situation, which is great! As is mentioned in the book, so much of blind people in literature are seen as people who are too weak to do anything for themselves, or they go completely the opposite direction and make them superheroes (Daredevil). There isn't a big panic about her being blind, but rather we just see her being brave. We see her fly seven hours to get to America with only herself and her little brother, but rather than thinking she's brave for doing this because she's blind, we think she's brave for doing this because she's SIXTEEN and uh, may have committed fraud. <br /><br />2. That we really got to take a <b>look into Laureth's mind,</b> and see what an everyday was like for her. She brought up the idea that it truly doesn't matter that much to her that she's 'missing out' on something. She's never been able to see different colours so why should she obsess over something that isn't going to happen? We can't see molecules (unless we use the super strong microscope that they just made), but only a portion of us actually invest our time into it. I would be completely fine if I never saw a life - it probably wouldn't make a difference to me. <i>ps. please let me know if this view is kind of narrow minded</i><br /><br />3. <b>Benjamin was such a sweetheart.</b> He was so good at helping his sister around, and knowing what to do. He was just the cutest, but at the same time he was so smart? It wasn't like he was a 20 year old in a 7 years olds body, he was definitely 7; rather he was an intelligent 7 year old but with all of the whining that comes with them. I love how he talked to his stuffed raven as well! That was so adorable, especially when Laureth was trying to get him to do something.</blockquote><br /><br />What Could Have Been Better<br /><blockquote>1. Occasionally the <b>journal extracts</b> seemed a little bit . . . unnecessary. I have a feeling that if I had skipped a few, I would still be able to understand the entire story. While it's true, there was ONE passage that was extremely relevant to the book, apart from that I couldn't find too much use for them.</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_910743340" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/910743340" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/910743340?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=diversity">diversity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer910743340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6796975200427159675">Exploring obsessions, coincidences, blindness and what it means to be family, She is Not Invisible is a mixed bag when it comes to ideas.<br/><br/>Having never read a Marcus Sedgwick book, I didn't have any expectations going in, and I can say I was pleasantly surprised. I was immediately sucked into the story of Laureth and her 7 year old brother, running away to New York to find her dad who she believes has gone missing. <br/><br/>I loved the insight into her thoughts and actions as someone who is blind. I really</span>
  <span id="freeText6796975200427159675" style="display:none">Exploring obsessions, coincidences, blindness and what it means to be family, She is Not Invisible is a mixed bag when it comes to ideas.<br /><br />Having never read a Marcus Sedgwick book, I didn't have any expectations going in, and I can say I was pleasantly surprised. I was immediately sucked into the story of Laureth and her 7 year old brother, running away to New York to find her dad who she believes has gone missing. <br /><br />I loved the insight into her thoughts and actions as someone who is blind. I really sensed the extra consideration she had to go through, trying to appear more confident than she felt, pretending to stare at objects and nodding at people even though she technically couldn't see their reactions. Seeing the world through how she navigated it was also interesting.<br /><br />The sibling relationship here was adorable and I really felt for her brother Benjamin at times. He actually acts like a 7 year old, with his imaginary pet Raven. Although I did have to suspend disbelief at his "power" and felt there was no explanation as to why he had it, which almost gave it a sci-fi twist which was a bit too convenient.<br /><br />There were so many disbeliefs that I had here, which kind of took me out of the story. A 16 year old travels countries with her young brother and somehow manages to leave the airport with no passport for her brother and nowhere to stay. Her mum only realises they are gone after a few days and makes 1 phone call. Combined with Benjamin's power and all the coincidences that happened, it just felt... unbelievable.<br /><br />The philosophical thoughts were interesting, especially exploring theories and causality of physics and coincidences, but after the 4th time these physicists were mentioned, my eyes kind of glazed over. As it explores their life and theories, it actually gets a bit too overwhelming. I also felt like a lot of it actually went over my head. <br /><br />After the build up of the whole book, and so many loose ends, I felt like the ending was anti-climactic and kind of pointless. I enjoyed the book at the start, got a bit lost in the middle, and was disappointed in the end. Definitely a mixed bag for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6796975200427159675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/932190510?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan  (thebookishtwins)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan  (thebookishtwins)" href="/user/show/12484735-megan-thebookishtwins">Megan  (thebookishtwins)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484735-megan-thebookishtwins?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484735-megan-thebookishtwins?shelf=not-in-usa-or-american-protaganist">not-in-usa-or-american-protaganist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484735-megan-thebookishtwins?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer932190510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13396300913707524597">I am a fan of Marcus Sedgwick ever since I read <i>Blood Red, Snow White</i> and I have been slowly making my way through his books. <i>She Is Not Invisible</i> is written fairly simple that makes for an easy read, and allows you to easily get to know the characters. I think this is a <b>great</b> book, especially as it adds light on how society reacts to disabled people, and those who are visually impaired and the protagonist Laureth Peak is blind. Therefore <i>She Is Not Invisible</i> adds some <b>diversity and originality</b> </span>
  <span id="freeText13396300913707524597" style="display:none">I am a fan of Marcus Sedgwick ever since I read <i>Blood Red, Snow White</i> and I have been slowly making my way through his books. <i>She Is Not Invisible</i> is written fairly simple that makes for an easy read, and allows you to easily get to know the characters. I think this is a <b>great</b> book, especially as it adds light on how society reacts to disabled people, and those who are visually impaired and the protagonist Laureth Peak is blind. Therefore <i>She Is Not Invisible</i> adds some <b>diversity and originality</b> to the YA contemporary genre, which is really great. Some great characters, with some good development and relationships with a nice mystery thrown in. <br /><br />Overall, an enjoyable and refreshing read. </span>

<div id="review_2249474912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2249474912" />
    <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes"><img alt="aPriL does feral sometimes " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478243665p2/3409532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2249474912?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="aPriL does feral sometimes " href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes">aPriL does feral sometimes </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781596438019" href="/book/show/17934419-she-is-not-invisible">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=edgy-but-still-a-cozy">edgy-but-still-a-cozy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=mysteries-potboilers-thrillers">mysteries-potboilers-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2249474912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15300191566642479358">'She is Not Invisible' is too young and too meh for me. The publisher and libraries appear to be calling the novel appropriate for young adults and teens, but I would think 4th graders would most enjoy the story. <br/><br/>Sixteen-year-old Laureth Peak, the narrator, is blind. She impulsively decides to travel by herself with her seven-year-old brother Benjamin on an airline from London to New York to find her missing father, Jack Peak, a writer of humorous books. When she tried to discuss her worry about</span>
  <span id="freeText15300191566642479358" style="display:none">'She is Not Invisible' is too young and too meh for me. The publisher and libraries appear to be calling the novel appropriate for young adults and teens, but I would think 4th graders would most enjoy the story. <br /><br />Sixteen-year-old Laureth Peak, the narrator, is blind. She impulsively decides to travel by herself with her seven-year-old brother Benjamin on an airline from London to New York to find her missing father, Jack Peak, a writer of humorous books. When she tried to discuss her worry about her missing father, a concern she built up after he did not answer his phone for several days, with her mother, her mom did not care where Jack was. <br /><br />Laureth had noticed a growing coolness between her mom and dad, especially as Jack's obsession with coincidences and the number 354 began to take over Jack's life 24/7. As Jack's obsessions grew, his books became more serious and his sales fell off. <br /><br />Ben helps Laureth navigate, but since Laureth is telling the story we readers get an insider look at being blind. As she takes taxis, goes through airports, handles two currencies and travels around the streets and boroughs of New York City, following clues her father left in a notebook which was found by another kid, she learns to trust herself in overcoming many obstacles. As the two children visit various locations, they meet interesting people and find themselves in a few dangerous situations.<br /><br />Their various adventures are interrupted by moments of reading Jack's notebook for clues. Jack wrote a great deal about what he had been learning about coincidences. Famous mathematically-inclined people and early psychoanalysts such as Jung and Freud had explored if coincidences demonstrated some principle behind the way the universe works, and maybe whatever 'it' was, if 'it' links up with human minds in some way. <br /><br />Frankly, gentle reader, these notebook musings of Jack's researches into the 'science' of coincidences was a bizarre interjection into the plot. Readers are introduced to some famous psychoanalysts and briefly we discover how they defined and named certain mental conditions surrounding the experience of coincidences (I myself lost my faith in religion after taking a Statistics class in college - hehe). Jack's journal also discusses the mind's natural and automatic seeking of patterns in everything. We do it in cataloguing faces to seeing coincidences to feeling numbers must be lucky if they keep turning up in our lives. I think the author wanted to show how Laureth used her father's patterns of thought as a guide to track him, but omg, gentle reader! If so, it was a very very very tenous link! She mostly used hard facts from informants, not coincidences, although a coincidence occurs. Even now, in thinking about this novel, I still do not understand why the author Marcus Sedgwick included in-depth material about coincidences in this book which is otherwise a basic mystery for elementary school kids. Plus, in the way the author discusses coincidences and patterns, I could not for the life of me figure out how it all related to Laureth's blindness or her adventure.<br /><br />My two reactions after finishing 'She is Not Invisible' were "whaaaat?" and 'meh'. I am giving an extra star for the insider view of Laureth's life as a blind person, even though it was a bit light in weight and brief in actual descriptions (barely any mention or use of Braille - to me, clearly a missed opportunity to discuss perceived patterns! - Laureth mostly uses Apple's Siri to read to her); however, this is a very simple book with an entertaining mystery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15300191566642479358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1107084429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1107084429" />
    <a title="Michelle Wrona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15162465-michelle-wrona"><img alt="Michelle Wrona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576510116p2/15162465.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1107084429?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Wrona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Wrona" href="/user/show/15162465-michelle-wrona">Michelle Wrona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781780621340" href="/book/show/21248666-she-is-not-invisible">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=weird">weird</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=it-is-just-me">it-is-just-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=sorry-not-sorry">sorry-not-sorry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=expected-better">expected-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=would-never-pick-up-again">would-never-pick-up-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=mystery-thriller-murder">mystery-thriller-murder</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=sisterly-brotherly-love">sisterly-brotherly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1107084429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17498820080731493307"><blockquote> "Love is a funny thing, and once again I really don't mean it's amusing. I mean it's odd. Strange. Weird. There was a time not so long ago, because I can remember it, when Mum and Dad loved each other. It was obvious, in the things that they did, and the way they were, and the way they called each other 'honey'." </blockquote><br/><br/> In the end of 2013, I came up to finding a list on Buzzfeed that showed the top twenty books that will sure be hits of 2014. This one was actually on it, and I've been wanting to read</span>
  <span id="freeText17498820080731493307" style="display:none"><blockquote> "Love is a funny thing, and once again I really don't mean it's amusing. I mean it's odd. Strange. Weird. There was a time not so long ago, because I can remember it, when Mum and Dad loved each other. It was obvious, in the things that they did, and the way they were, and the way they called each other 'honey'." </blockquote><br><br> In the end of 2013, I came up to finding a list on Buzzfeed that showed the top twenty books that will sure be hits of 2014. This one was actually on it, and I've been wanting to read it for the longest time. Where in the world would you find a mysterious thriller showing the point of view of a young blind girl?<br><br> I must say that I was pretty disappointed with this one, compared to all of the wonderful things said about Marcus Sedgwick and his writing. You may say I was the black sheep, but I'm actually very glad to have had the experience to read such a novel with a fantastic concept. There were just the minor things that set me off and disappointed me. Other than that, I was as happy as a sheep getting its wool shaved off. Okay, I'm over exaggerating about that joke there. But, you get what I mean.<br><br> Sedgwick is an <i>excellent writer,</i> don't get me wrong. He has a majestic way of captivating readers with his crazy but believable concepts, and you feel like you want to get to know the characters so well that they'll be your new best buddies.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397928277ra/9347688.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> This is about exactly what I first mentioned. Laureth and her brother are off to New York from their home in England to find their father—since Laureth received an email stating that someone's found her father's notebook—one that he's sure to never lose or forget anywhere. <br><br> Did I mention that Laureth's blind and her brother is so young and they're off in the unknown? No, not really. <br><br> That's basically the simple plot, but it made a huge difference and the meaning is so deep and found and relieved with gorgeousness. The concept was actually something I never really had a strong encounter with and I must say that <i> whatshisname Sedgwick </i> has stunned me in that aspect and is sure to stun millions of others who are willing to begin reading a contemporary that is <b>so strange in its nice way.</b><br><br><blockquote> "Sight must have its advantages. Like, I'm never going to drive a car, well not on public roads at least. But I can live with that. I've never wanted to be able to see, not really, but right then I knew that if I could see, I wouldn't have had to bring Benjamin with me, and then, I felt awful." </blockquote> <br><br> The book stayed the same way the whole time through. I felt the same thing from beginning to end, and there weren't any omg-so-amazing moments as I expected there'd be. I sat there after finishing, thinking, <b>
  <i>"Why wasn't this to my advantage in any way?"</i>
</b> I wanted more jazz, and more action. Was this really supposed to be a hardcore mystery?<br><br> Laureth was honestly awesome. Because of her disability, I wasn't feeling intended to feel guilty, she just had us reading in a whole new perspective, <i>from the eyes of a blind person.</i> At the same time, she didn't intend to feel sorry for herself either, and she cared about the people around her. Just look at the risks she took to keep her brother safe and to find her father. She was honestly a dreamer and I loved her personality and self-being. Her attitude was a hit.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417655941ra/12470076.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But throughout this whole "journey" or "story" or whatever you intend to call this novel, my favourite character remaining throughout had to be little Benjamin, Laureth's brother. He was such a perfect spirit and was so adorable! You don't really realize it until the end, but he made a total difference in Laureth's life and helped solve the mystery quicker than she could've ever imagined.<br><br> And one last thing—did you know that this book had to do with books? A lot of crazy awesome things were mentioned about fiction and coincidences, and I just loved it. This book was my environment at moments, but I wanted more.<br><br><blockquote> 'Yes,' said Dad. 'Oh. Coincidences in fiction just do not work. And even in real life, they tend to fall into two sorts. The ones that are so pathetic that they don't excite anyone but you, and the ones that are so incredible that they are literally just that; unbelievable. Even to members of your own family.' </blockquote><br><br> Huh—I don't know. Do you ever get a feeling that you knew what was going to happen but then you didn't really know? Of course you did—that's what I was feeling with this book. I wish that I could've seen <i>fireworks and sparks</i> with my love, but this mystery wasn't everything I was planning it to be. I did love and enjoy the culture and impact on readers, though!<br><br>This review can also be found on <a href="http://thatgirlybookworm.blogspot.ca/2014/12/she-is-not-invisible-by-marcus-sedgwick.html" rel="nofollow noopener">A Thousand Lives Lived,</a> check it out for more reviews!e<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17498820080731493307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_849214045" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/849214045" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8167267-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481158927p2/8167267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/849214045?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/8167267-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8167267-andrea?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8167267-andrea?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8167267-andrea?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8167267-andrea?shelf=arc-netgalley">arc-netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer849214045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16305522806829344003">DNF at 50%.<br/><br/>I tried. I really did. I struggled at lot with the beginning of the book but gave myself a goal of reaching at least 50% before giving up. Sometimes books have rough starts but develop into amazing stories. Unfortunatelly it wasn't the same with this book. <br/><br/>I'm not really sure how to review because it's not a <i>bad</i> book, it just... isn't my kind of book. It has an interesting story but the narrative and the execution just didn't work for me.<br/><br/>Laureth is a 16 year old whose father's noteboo</span>
  <span id="freeText16305522806829344003" style="display:none">DNF at 50%.<br /><br />I tried. I really did. I struggled at lot with the beginning of the book but gave myself a goal of reaching at least 50% before giving up. Sometimes books have rough starts but develop into amazing stories. Unfortunatelly it wasn't the same with this book. <br /><br />I'm not really sure how to review because it's not a <i>bad</i> book, it just... isn't my kind of book. It has an interesting story but the narrative and the execution just didn't work for me.<br /><br />Laureth is a 16 year old whose father's notebook shows up in the USA when he was supposed to be in Europe. Laureth is worried but her mother won't listen to her, so to help her father she takes her 7 year old brother on a cross world trip to find out what happened. <br /><br />When I read the premise I was instantly interested. A blind girl using her brain and her little brother as a guide to uncover the mystery of their father's disappearance. I thought it'd be an interesting mystery book, with an even more interesting character, but Laureth just disappointed me. She's 16, but has the voice of a child and her immaturity just threw me off the story. Her father is away on a business trip and she only finds out something is strange because she gets an e-mail from a person in the USA saying they found her father's notebook. Then for the first time in days - in over a week- she tries to get in touch and gets no answer. She tells her mother, who seems to realize something is wrong but tells Laureth to not worry. I just don't understand why Laureth would consider going to the USA instead of going to the police first. Her father is supposed to be in Europe. He hasn't gotten in touch in days. There's no answer and she calls and then it goes to voice mail. He's basically gone. That's enough to at least <i>try</i> the police. Instead she purchases plane tickets and travels halfway around the world, kidnapping her little brother. <br /><br />I'm usually pretty open minded when I'm reading fiction, but sometimes I need to smallest hint of reality because I can suspend my belief only so much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16305522806829344003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/765918664?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9781780621333" href="/book/show/19081787-she-is-not-invisible">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5740882-books-are-tardis?shelf=harriet-the-spy-esque">harriet-the-spy-esque</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5740882-books-are-tardis?shelf=awesome-siblings">awesome-siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5740882-books-are-tardis?shelf=awesome-dad-award">awesome-dad-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5740882-books-are-tardis?shelf=you-ve-got-mail">you-ve-got-mail</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5740882-books-are-tardis?shelf=philosophical-musings">philosophical-musings</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer765918664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16812036670493038187">This is a quirky and fast paced read which highlights a rarely discussed topic in YA: visual impairment. And the way this topic is handled is both brave and enlightening. It features a wonderful sibling relationship and a fascinating author dad. I love meta books like these, this one not only features an author dad and his books, but the process of writing books. It also features at great length scientific research on the phenomenon of coincidences (which I very much feel like calling co-inky-di</span>
  <span id="freeText16812036670493038187" style="display:none">This is a quirky and fast paced read which highlights a rarely discussed topic in YA: visual impairment. And the way this topic is handled is both brave and enlightening. It features a wonderful sibling relationship and a fascinating author dad. I love meta books like these, this one not only features an author dad and his books, but the process of writing books. It also features at great length scientific research on the phenomenon of coincidences (which I very much feel like calling co-inky-dinks now). All the science in this book is just wonderful. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384263286ra/6829874.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432378655ra/14948370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The pseudo-spiritual and philosophical discussion over coincidences kept me reeled in. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404607249ra/10263654.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432378789ra/14948418.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I really liked Laureth and sympathized with her storyline in the book, without EVER feeling sorry for her, which I like to think is the point.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432378655ra/14948372.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>She's a bit of a worrier and puts such a brave face on for the world while questioning and doubting herself inside, it was so very relate-able, especially the worrying to death part.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432378655ra/14948373.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Anyone who has ever had an all-consuming joins all the dots of your life kind of personal epiphany would find in this book, a kindred spirit. Personal epiphanies can take you on the wildest goose-chases, sometimes for the better and sometimes for the worse. This is one of those books that will either be a hit or a miss, and for me, it was a complete hit, for the love of science.</span>

<div id="review_751235861" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/751235861" />
    <a title="Deborah Swift" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3493727-deborah-swift"><img alt="Deborah Swift" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457690786p2/3493727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/751235861?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Swift" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Swift" href="/user/show/3493727-deborah-swift">Deborah Swift</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer751235861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18138240535570526115">I am a big Marcus Sedgwick fan so expected a lot of this novel. Where it succeeds brilliantly is in giving us a real insight into what it must be like to be blind, so much so that you actually feel that sense of continually groping to find things other sighted people take for granted. The characterisation is excellent and Laureth and Benjamin very believable. Where the book is not so strong for me is in the notebooks of the father - as Jack Peak rightly points out, other people's coincidences ar</span>
  <span id="freeText18138240535570526115" style="display:none">I am a big Marcus Sedgwick fan so expected a lot of this novel. Where it succeeds brilliantly is in giving us a real insight into what it must be like to be blind, so much so that you actually feel that sense of continually groping to find things other sighted people take for granted. The characterisation is excellent and Laureth and Benjamin very believable. Where the book is not so strong for me is in the notebooks of the father - as Jack Peak rightly points out, other people's coincidences are not as exciting as your own. Although I wanted to engage with all the material in Jack Peak's writer's notebook, I found myself inclined to skip over it to get to the action of the plot. Although it informed, it also seemed to interrupt the narrative.Some of it I thought a seven year old boy would have a lot of trouble reading out. I also found the explanation for Jack Peak's disappearance a bit of an anticlimax - these you would think would spoil my enjoyment....<br /><br />BUT this book asks lots of questions about writing - such as how much of a coincidence is too much when creating a believable plot,and should a writer write to please himself or his fans? So any perceived weaknesses in the writing are reflected back to the reader as questions about what makes a successful novel.I thoroughly recommend this as a book which will make you think, and even better, make you ask questions about books and the nature of coincidence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18138240535570526115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_879613715" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/879613715" />
    <a title="Ksenia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/825809-ksenia"><img alt="Ksenia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388351518p2/825809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/879613715?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ksenia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ksenia" href="/user/show/825809-ksenia">Ksenia</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781596438019" href="/book/show/17934419-she-is-not-invisible">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/825809-ksenia?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer879613715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17731965966771894305">The beauty of this book is that you truly get to experience Laureth's journey, with Laureth. Because of her blindness and first-person narration, you get to experience the world "through her eyes," and that's where Marcus is most excellent at his craft. Marcus is, simply put, a master storyteller! If he writes it, I will read it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3361694619" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3361694619" />
    <a title="Fiona Daley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/100999409-fiona-daley"><img alt="Fiona Daley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579063660p2/100999409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3361694619?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fiona Daley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fiona Daley" href="/user/show/100999409-fiona-daley">Fiona Daley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3361694619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12757890330678548474">I loved this book! It is a fun thriller/adventure. One thing I especially love is that the struggles in this book are so real. I love Marcus Sedwick's writing, and the writing of the writer in the book. I love the relationship of the sister and brother, the family relationships, and the struggles of the girl trying to prove she is not invisible. A great read for sure! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QCmf1+m6GTpdUm0HIkK+mkF/1QDyvs/BwsvFgVAUSA68wVxFWbStjR7oecY9tusoCe1FrN35I/ExfAdz0NX7EA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ta5GZCwuqQD5/lpglhhoR/way42MB3ujooFEggJUYl1JRoX2nCAdt7pETqGJ7D31tIhbIaNAl5NRNoZwgpXRQw==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1348088975490443143">Marcus Sedgwick was born in Kent, England. Marcus is a British author and illustrator as well as a musician. He is the author of several books, including <i>Witch Hill</i> and <i>The Book of Dead Days</i>, both of which were nominated for the Edgar Allan Poe Award. The most recent of these nominations rekindled a fascination with Poe that has borne fruit here in (in <i>The Restless Dead</i>, 2007) the form of "The Hea</span>
  <span id="freeText1348088975490443143" style="display:none">Marcus Sedgwick was born in Kent, England. Marcus is a British author and illustrator as well as a musician. He is the author of several books, including <i>Witch Hill</i> and <i>The Book of Dead Days</i>, both of which were nominated for the Edgar Allan Poe Award. The most recent of these nominations rekindled a fascination with Poe that has borne fruit here in (in <i>The Restless Dead</i>, 2007) the form of "The Heart of Another" - inspired by Poe's "The Tell-Tale Heart." Of his story, Sedgwick says, "This was one of those stories that I thought might be a novel originally but actually was much better suited to the tight form of the short story. I had the initial idea some years ago but was just waiting for the right ingredient to come along. Poe's story, as well as his own fascination with technique, provided that final piece of the puzzle."<br /><br />He used to play for two bands namely playing the drums for Garrett and as the guitarist in an ABBA tribute group. He has published novels such as <i>Floodland</i> (winner of the Branford Boase Award in 2001) and <i>The Dark Horse</i> (shortlisted for The Guardian Children's Book Award 2002).</span>
  <a data-text-id="1348088975490443143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/24963141-she-is-not-invisible">Quotes from She Is Not Invisible</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;People think I have so much faith in myself, but I have none. I have no faith in myself, or in what I can do, and yet people think I can do anything I want.<br />That's how I seem, but it's an illusion. It's an act, nothing more.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1217735-people-think-i-have-so-much-faith-in-myself-but">16 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;How do you find a name?" <br />"In this case, on a shampoo bottle. It's one of the ingredients; Sodium Laureth Sulphate. He thought it was a beautiful word and sounded like a name."<br />"He's right."<br />"Mum didn't think so. He swears he told her at the time where it came from, and maybe he did, but she was too ill to remember. I was seven when she found out, and then she hit the roof. 'You named our daughter after a chemical!' That kind of thing."<br />"I still think it's a cool name," said Sam, and I could hear the smile in his voice. It was a soft voice, too. I liked it.<br />"And very beautiful," he added.<br />"Thank you," I said, feeling a little warm inside. <br />"And that's why I have such a boring name," said Benjamin.<br />"Oh, hey," said Sam. "That's a cool name, too."<br />"No, it's not," said Benjamin. "There are two Bens in my class. Mum said she was going to choose my name when I was born. Dad wasn't allowed. So I got a boring name. But that's why Stan's called Stan."<br />"Because you wanted him to have a boring name, too?"<br />"Stan's not a boring name. It's short for Stannous."<br />"Stannous?" <br />"Stannous Chloride," I said. "It's a chemical. It was on a tube of toothpaste."<br />Sam laughed. <br />"Mum hit the roof," said Benjamin, proudly.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1217688-how-do-you-find-a-name-in-this-case-on">11 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
